Local News

Central Constitutional Draft Review Committee Invites Wang Chonghui to Beijing by Telegram; Wang Declines Due to Doctor's Orders

The Central Constitutional Draft Review Committee held a meeting in Beijing on the 18th. The committee considers Mr. Wang Chonghui, a member of the Central Committee currently residing in Shanghai due to illness, to be an expert in law. Ye Chucang, the convener of the committee, has come to Shanghai twice to exchange opinions with Mr. Wang. According to Mr. Wang's secretary, Xiao Jinfang, speaking to a Central News Agency reporter, the committee will continue its meeting in Beijing on the 23rd. Therefore, on the evening of the 17th, a telegram was sent inviting Mr. Wang to go to Beijing on the 22nd to attend the meeting on the 23rd and discuss all matters. After receiving the telegram, Mr. Wang originally intended to go to Beijing as scheduled. However, due to his chronic illness requiring continued treatment in Shanghai, he feared he would not recover in time. Following his doctor's orders and to prevent a relapse, he was unable to accept the invitation to go to Beijing and attend the meeting. He has already replied to the committee by telegram, it is said. It is also learned that Mr. Wang went to Dr. Huang Bingji's clinic on Beijing Road yesterday morning to treat a dental ailment, returning to his residence at noon.

Southwest Elders Telegraph Shanghai, Contributing Opinions on the Constitutional Draft

According to the New News Agency, Sun Ke, Wang Chonghui, Cheng Tianku, et al. continued their discussions yesterday afternoon. Various central figures such as Sun Ke, Ye Chucang, Dai Chuanxian, Ju Zheng, and Chen Bulei have repeatedly exchanged opinions with Dr. Wang Chonghui, a Chinese legal expert in Shanghai, regarding the amendment of the constitutional draft and the addition of transitional provisions. It is reported that the elders of the Southwest have also frequently telegraphed various important figures in Shanghai recently to discuss the above issues. At 4:30 PM yesterday afternoon, Sun Ke, the President of the Legislative Yuan, visited Dr. Wang Chonghui at the Hu residence on Gaen Road again to continue exchanging opinions on the revision of the constitutional draft. Also present were Cheng Tianku, representing Mr. Hu Hanmin, and former Minister of Justice and lawyer Zhang Shizhao. The discussion lasted for over an hour before they took their leave one after another. Dr. Wang Zhengting, a member of the Central Committee and former Minister of Foreign Affairs, also drove to visit Mr. Wang Chonghui at 5:30 PM yesterday afternoon, departing after a half-hour conversation.

Sun Ke and Kong Xiangxi Arrive in Shanghai Yesterday Morning

Sun Ke, the President of the Legislative Yuan, and Kong Xiangxi, the Vice President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, arrived in Shanghai together at 7:15 AM yesterday morning on the overnight express train from Beijing. After getting off at the Zhenru Railway Station, they each returned to their private residences to rest. Kong Xiangxi went to the Central Bank at around 11:00 AM to handle official business and meet with leaders of the banking community, scheduling a return to Beijing on the overnight train next Monday to preside over the Executive Yuan meeting. Sun Ke rested briefly at his private residence before going out to handle private matters, planning to stay in Shanghai for a few days before returning to Beijing.

Kong Xiangrong Comes to Shanghai to Discuss; Reasons for the Rapid Closure of the Dongzhuang Breach - Over Two Million Yuan Saved in Expenses

The Dongzhuang breach on the Yellow River caused disaster in seventeen counties in western Shandong and northern Jiangsu. The closure project has now been completed. Yesterday, Kong Xiangrong, the acting chairman of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission, came to Shanghai and discussed the breach closure in great detail. The following is a narrative account. According to Mr. Kong,

Since the Yellow River Conservancy Commission took over the Dongzhuang breach closure, it was fortunate to be completed in less than three months. The closure work was also completed in a very short time, just before the Qingming Festival, without delaying the spring plowing of the people, and without violating the order of Minister Kong, a standing committee member of the Economic Commission and in charge of national water conservancy affairs, which is gratifying. When I, Kong Xiangrong, took over, the breach had completely diverted the river's flow, making construction difficult. The funds allocated by the central government to the previous breach committee had already been exhausted, making it even more difficult to continue without funds. At that time, Minister Kong firmly instructed that the closure be completed before Qingming, so as not to delay agricultural activities. However, he assumed full responsibility for planning the necessary funds. He first allocated 300,000 yuan to maintain the status quo during the transition between the old and new administrations and to prevent the interruption of labor and materials. He then vigorously presided over the allocation of 3 million yuan in public bonds, establishing 1.5 million yuan in cash through mortgages in less than ten days. The financial situation was extremely urgent at the time, but with the assistance of the Central Bank and the mediation of Shandong Provincial Chairman Han, it was ultimately successful. Furthermore, when there was an urgent need for funds for the excavation of the diversion channel, Mr. Kong approved my telegram requesting an additional 300,000 yuan to meet the urgent need, allowing those in charge to cope adequately and quickly close the breach. However, I, Kong Xiangrong, always mindful of the central government's difficulty in raising funds, sought to economize and economize again. It is estimated that by the time the closure was completed, more than one million yuan of material costs had been saved compared to the approved budget. Furthermore, according to the labor and materials required for the actual implementation of the project, a supplementary budget should have been requested, but it was not requested. Instead, economizing within the original budget, another one million yuan was saved, totaling over two million yuan. This is what I, Kong Xiangrong, am gratified about. As for the main materials, such as straw and willow branches, the governments of Hebei, Shandong, and Henan provinces instructed the counties along the river to assist in purchasing and transporting labor. Regarding stone materials, Minister Kong, acting as Premier of the Executive Yuan, proposed and passed a resolution to allocate locomotives and trains from the Longhai, Jinpu, and other five railway bureaus to increase transportation capacity, so that materials were not lacking and the project could be carried out with peace of mind. This is another reason for the rapid closure. As for the engineering, the new willow-stone-jujube-sleeper method was adopted to close the breach, while the old-fashioned "楷掃" method was used to advance and close the breach. The most effective aspects were the extension of Jiangsu and the diversion of the flow northward, as well as the smooth flow of water through the old and new diversion channels, the maintenance and progress of the willow-stone slopes, the consolidation of the willow-stone-bundled sleepers, and the temporary heavy rewards to soldiers and laborers for their risk-taking and vigorous advancement, which was also a major reason for the early celebration of the closure. Currently, due to the unified Yellow River defense issue and Minister Kong's telegram to me, Kong Xiangrong, and the provincial governments of the three provinces to discuss post-disaster engineering in order to avoid the tragedy of another breach, I have come to Beijing to seek instructions and report on the emergency closure process, as well as to request approval for two items, which have all been approved. I will soon go to Jinan with Chief Engineer Zhu to discuss everything with Chairman Han. In addition to compiling a summary of the Dongzhuang Yellow River breach closure project for the reference of those concerned about Yellow River affairs, the original memorial will also be submitted. It is attached below. The Shandong Breach Committee's proposed budget for this Dongzhuang breach, which was approved, included a total of more than 3.48 million yuan for the breach closure and diversion channel expenses. Excluding what had already been used by the previous Breach Committee, it is estimated that by the date of completion of the breach closure, the commission had saved material expenses totaling over one million yuan. This is one item to report. The reason why this breach closure was able to save a large amount of money was that every blade of grass and tree was used effectively, and every "掃占" and "石占" that were made was a further step forward. Because the project did not suffer any losses, the Economic Commission reduced the original estimate of this embankment and advancement project by 900,000 yuan, on the grounds that "旱占" cannot be calculated in the same depth as "水占". However, what Shandong did was "旱占", while what our commission did was "水占". According to the completed "水占" project, 500,000 yuan should be added, but the commission economized on the sluice gate management and did not request a supplementary budget, which is equivalent to saving 500,000 yuan. This is the second item to report. The reason why the aforementioned "掃占", "石占", and "金門占" were able to be firmly secured was that the east and west dams on the riverside side of the embankments were all added with the "柳石坦坡" protection project. This project was not estimated by the previous Breach Committee. Now, 18,000 square feet of stone blocks have been purchased, and 10,000 square feet have been transported to Jinan for use. Compared to the approved budget, at least more than 500,000 yuan should be added, but the commission has economized on the original budget and purchased them without requesting a third supplement. This time, the closure was rapid, saving money and materials in large quantities, and it was largely due to the hard work of the staff. During the emergency closure and the critical moment of convergence, I, Kong Xiangrong, announced in public that if the closure could be completed today, the soldiers and laborers throwing willow bundles in the front line of the two dams would be awarded 2,000 yuan for each dam. The two section chiefs leading the soldiers and laborers who risked their lives would each be awarded 500 yuan. As expected, under the heavy reward, the soldiers and laborers did not care for themselves, and I, Kong Xiangrong, personally directed the work, and the closure was completed within four hours. The closure work was also due to the fact that during the closure of the side dam, the "夹土" at the "龍門口" was stimulated by the flow, which was turbulent and dangerous. I, Kong Xiangrong, supervised the soldiers and laborers on the two dams to vigorously advance and turned the danger into safety in an instant. The closure work was completed, and according to the example, the soldiers and laborers on the west and east dams were each awarded 500 yuan. This is the fourth item to report. The materials saved this time should be used for various embankment restoration and post-disaster projects in accordance with your previous telegram. The work has continued to be rushed forward without daring to stop. However, regarding the embankment restoration work in Shandong Province, it is necessary to personally discuss the handling with Chairman Han. Before the central government sends personnel to inspect and accept the work, I intend to rush to Jinan to discuss everything and ask whether I can make discretionary plans for work within the scope of the original approved budget for the breach closure. This is one item to request instructions for. This Dongzhuang project was huge, not comparable to Fenglou and Guantai. Transportation was difficult and construction was dangerous. All the personnel in various places were able to work hard. For more than two months in the past three months, they had not slept. Some vomited blood and some were seriously ill. I, Kong Xiangrong, could not bear it. Now, it is fortunate that the closure has been completed and the breach work has been completed, without delaying the spring plowing of the people. Can we follow the example of the Fenglou and Guantai breach closures and calculate all the original salaries and fees that the staff members in the work have contributed and give them two more months as a reward for their efforts? This is the second item to request instructions for. The reasonable thing is to draft a memorial to request review and instructions, and to follow them respectfully. Respectfully presented to Kong, Standing Committee Member and Director of the Water Conservancy Commission.

All Trade Unions in the City Gave a Farewell Banquet to Zhu Xuefan Yesterday; Over a Hundred Representatives Attended, with Enthusiastic Sentiments; Hosts and Guests Exchanged Speeches with Much Encouragement

According to the Da Gong News Agency, the trade unions of this city held a public farewell banquet yesterday noon at the Atlantic Restaurant for Zhu Xuefan, the representative of this year's National Labor Conference, and Zhao Banfu, the representative of the Maritime Conference. The following attended: Lu Jingshi, a member of the Municipal Party Committee; Zhou Xuexiang, Shao Xubai, Ye Xianggao, and Long Peiyun, standing committee members of the General Labor Union; Gong Yuting, Fan Yifeng, Zhang Kechang, Li Hua, Lu Muqin, Zhao Zhenhui, Zhang Zhuyun, Le Junwen, and other representatives from various trade unions in the four districts, including cigarette manufacturing, ink manufacturing, sauce making, tugboats, postal workers, postal staff, navigation, Anlu, the five districts, including match manufacturing, five districts, including cigarette manufacturing, military uniforms, tea making, five districts, including cotton spinning, car drivers, two districts, including water and electricity, wooden shipbuilding, civil ship shoulder bearers, hat making, one district, including water and electricity, candle industry, six districts, including knitting, six districts, including silk reeling, leather making, six districts, including water and electricity, dyeing, three districts, including cotton spinning, freight forwarding, water pipe engineering, pharmaceuticals, ten districts, including cotton spinning, special zone public buses, labor movement association, newspaper industry, six districts, including public buses, one district, including cleaning, two districts, including shipbuilding, toothbrushes, five districts, including carpentry, newspaper distribution, four districts, including rubber, "梗片", nine districts, including soap pharmaceuticals, four districts, including shipbuilding, one district, including shipbuilding, and over one hundred fifty guests and guests such as Ren Jinping, etc.

Chairman's Speech. During the meeting, Chairman Zhou Xuexiang delivered a farewell speech, stating in brief: "Comrade Zhu Xuefan is an advanced worker in the labor community. His spirit of leading the labor movement and working diligently for several years is worthy of our admiration. This time, being sent to attend the National Labor Conference, he will be able to negotiate and defend the interests of our country's laborers in the international arena and strive for equality in international status, while at the same time increasing the glory of our country's government. Comrade Zhao Banfu has a considerable history in the maritime field, and we are also confident that he will be able to strive for the welfare of all seafarers. We also hope that the two representatives will take the opportunity to attend the meeting to observe the construction of the United States and new countries, as well as the situation of their people's organizations, so that they can introduce them to the domestic labor community after returning to the country. Today, we have prepared a simple meal and held a public farewell banquet, and we offer a toast to wish the two gentlemen a safe journey."

Zhu Xuefan's Speech. Zhu then stood up and delivered a speech, saying: "This time, I have been appointed by the Central Committee to represent the 20th National Labor Conference, and I am ashamed of my talent and unable to shoulder the heavy responsibility. I am very grateful for the grand banquet held by the trade unions of this city to send me off. The International Labor Organization is an international labor organization established based on the Treaty of Peace, and its role is to eliminate the injustice, hardship, poverty, and various inhuman systems of the majority of people in the world through international cooperation, maintain and improve the living standards of workers, and establish a permanent peace and happiness in human society. At least one international labor conference is held every year, bringing together representatives from the government, employers, and labor of each member country to jointly discuss and resolve various labor issues. Since its establishment in 1919, there have been 19 conferences held, with 45 draft conventions and many recommendations passed. Therefore, it has made many contributions to the improvement of labor issues around the world, and its impact on the progress of international labor legislation is significant. In fact, it can be called the highest labor legislative body in the international arena. China is one of the countries that signed the Treaty of Peace, so it is also an original member of the International Labor Organization. Since 1929, it has begun to send complete delegations to attend, that is, representatives from the government, employers, and labor are all present at the conference. China is still an agricultural society, but in recent years, light industry has shown development. According to the latest estimates by the Labor Bureau, there are 30 million workers. In addition, handicraft workers and mobile workers are not included. Furthermore, due to the rapid collapse of the countryside in recent years, farmers have been forced to sell their labor in cities, forming a surplus of labor. The new industries have been devastated by international economic aggression, not only unable to develop, but also unable to maintain their original foundation, and have stopped working and reduced labor one after another. As a result, the number of unemployed has increased sharply. According to the above estimates, there are already 5,893,000 unemployed workers among the number of workers, causing the current unstable situation. Therefore, China's labor problem has obviously reached a very serious level, and the degree to which it needs to be resolved is also very urgent, and there is much reliance on international cooperation and assistance. Modern international relations are becoming increasingly close, and any issue is related to the international community. Only through open international discussions, abandoning racial, class, and political prejudices, can an accurate and effective solution be obtained. You and I are all Chinese workers, and we ourselves are direct victims of the unreasonable system. We have the most practical experience of the suffering and needs of Chinese workers. I will do my best at this conference to arouse international attention and sympathy, so that they can update their views on China. The most painful thing for Chinese workers at present, apart from the economic aspect, is the cruel and harsh treatment of Chinese workers by foreigners who set up factories in China, such as refusing factory inspections by the Chinese government, neglecting protective facilities, disregarding workers' interests, and not allowing workers to form associations and meetings, which is most embarrassing for us. The right to association and assembly is a basic right of the people in modern civilized countries, and the International Labor Organization Charter and Chinese laws have clear provisions. This right cannot be deprived by any force. However, foreigners in Chinese concessions openly prohibit Chinese workers from forming trade unions, do not recognize our worker representatives, and do not abide by Chinese laws. We can hardly tolerate this point any longer. I intend to submit this to the conference and request the National Labor Conference to make a fair ruling. In addition, there is the issue that domestic workers and foreign workers should receive equal treatment. In this world economic panic, countries have adopted the policy of excluding foreign workers as a result of the recession. In recent years, the tragic situation of various countries排斥 Chinese workers has been seen even now. There are still a huge number of Chinese workers who have been forced to become unemployed and are wandering in foreign lands. I have already drafted a proposal on this point, requesting the conference to take effective measures. In addition, I also plan to raise issues concerning requesting various countries to assist China in prohibiting opium and poison, as well as our country's unemployment problem and the dumping of foreign goods. Here, we must have an understanding that China's labor problem cannot be separated from international relations and solved independently. However, it is also unreliable to rely solely on the help of others. Only by relying on ourselves can we overcome difficulties. At the same time, we must recognize the characteristics of China's labor problem, which from the beginning includes the nature of national resistance. In other words, China's labor problem is China's national liberation problem. Therefore, while seeking the liberation of the workers themselves, we must not neglect the importance of national rejuvenation. We must unite and work hard, and only in this way can the liberation and happiness of the workers be guaranteed permanently and strongly. In recent years, the active progress of the Chinese labor movement has been a very gratifying thing. Most Chinese workers have considerable organizations. According to statistics from the Central Civil Movement Steering Committee, in 1934, the number of Chinese trade unions was 458. In fact, there are still many omissions, and they are all actively striving for the road to national restoration under the leadership of our party. This kind of resolute and courageous spirit is one of the greatest forces. This force will undoubtedly become an important element in the rejuvenation of the Chinese nation. However, we should not be complacent, but should strive for progress and perfection in order to complete this glorious historical mission. I am representing Chinese workers to attend the conference this time, and I am a servant of all of you present and the workers of the whole country. All of you present are leaders of the Shanghai labor community, and I am sure that you will provide good opinions. I also hope that the comrades of the national labor community will give instructions and correct my shortcomings at any time. That is what I hope for."

Representative's Speech. Zhao Banfu then gave a thank-you speech, briefly stating that he felt that his knowledge was shallow and that he was not competent enough to attend the Maritime Conference this time, but he was honored by the summoning of the leaders of various trade unions and felt even more ashamed. This time, going abroad, he would follow Mr. Xuefan and do his best to strive for the happiness of seafarers. Today, participating in the farewell banquet, in addition to expressing his gratitude to everyone, he also hoped that everyone would give him advice at any time. Then, Lu Jingshi, a member of the Municipal Party Committee, Ren Jinping, a guest, and Shao Xubai, a standing committee member of the General Labor Union, successively gave speeches. The general idea was that they hoped that the two representatives would work hard in the international arena and strive for national power, rejuvenate the Chinese nation, and then Chinese workers would be able to obtain true liberation.

Chairman's Report: After formal greetings, Chairman Wang Xiaolai reported, stating that today's meeting continues the 15th First Representative Assembly to conduct a supplemental election of one Chinese committee member to attend the Shanghai Municipal Council, elect 27 executive committee members, and discuss various proposals. At the previous meeting, the re-election of Wang Yansong and Wu Yunzhai did not result in either receiving a majority of votes. Therefore, according to regulations, another election is held today. However, both Mr. Wang and Mr. Wu sent letters stating that due to their busy schedules and public affairs, they are unable to serve as a committee member and do not wish to be considered. The chairman read the two letters aloud, and the entire assembly unanimously approved their request and granted their withdrawal.

Election of Chinese Committee Member: After the chairman's report, ballots were distributed to elect one Chinese committee member. Cao Zhigong and Li Wenjie were appointed as vote counters, and Xie Zhongfu and He Wuliang as vote callers. The election resulted in Zhou Yueran receiving 56 votes, thus being elected as a committee member. Zhou is a native of Wuxing, 52 years old, and formerly a teacher at Jiangsu Higher School, director of the English department at Nanjing Higher Normal School, and a co-examiner for the third Higher Civil Service Examination of the Examination Yuan. He currently serves as an executive member of the Lake Society and vice-principal of the Commercial Press Correspondence School.

The chairman appointed Zhang Juansheng, Xu Guanqun, Yu Chuanding, and Chen Ziming as vote counters, and Qiu Jialiang, Yu Yaoqiu, Wang Jingdong, and Feng Bingxun as vote callers. The following nine individuals were elected as alternate executive committee members: Li Zhiyun (29 votes), Xie Xiaochu (29 votes), Wang Jingdong (28 votes), Gu Wensheng (28 votes), Sun Wuqi (28 votes), Zhu Hegao (27 votes), Wang Haifan (27 votes), Chen Ziming (26 votes), and Xu Guanqun (26 votes).

Page 10

Passed Eight Proposals

After the chairman announced the list of elected executive committee members, the discussion of various proposals commenced as follows: (A) Requesting the Municipal Government and authorizing the Municipal Council to promptly negotiate with relevant countries to agree that the Municipal Council increase the number of Chinese directors by four seats starting from the 26th year of the Republic to show greater cooperation. Resolved: Passed. (B) Regarding the Shanghai Telephone Company's telephone rates, the four proposals put forward by the Chinese directors of the Municipal Council were amended to calculate each call at three cents, regardless of whether it is for commercial or residential use, or the basic number of calls. Resolved: In accordance with the report of the Telephone Special Committee (previously reported), to unite with various public organizations, expand the organization, and continue the protest. (C) Urging the Municipal Council to strictly implement the provision of the Yangjingbang Real Estate Regulations regarding the ratio of 20:1 between house tax and land tax, and that the house tax should not be an exception according to the regulations, and should be in accordance with the burden method implemented by the Shanghai Municipal Government. Resolved: Passed. (D) Again urging the Municipal Council to promptly compile all individual regulations into a booklet in Chinese and distribute it to the ratepayers. Resolved: Passed. (E) Questioning the Municipal Council as to why the proposal of this association to "abolish the band and the vehicle committee" has not been implemented. Resolved: Passed. (F) Questioning the Municipal Council as to why it has not implemented the resolution of this association last year that "starting from this year, the annual report, budget, and final accounts should be compiled in both Chinese and English and submitted to this association before April 1st for distribution to registered Chinese ratepayers for review by the representative assembly." Resolved: Passed. (G) Amending the term limit for Chinese directors and committee members. After Xu Jikui explained in detail, it was resolved to amend Article 1 of the rules for electing directors and committee members to attend the Municipal Council to read: "The Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Public Concession shall elect representatives (directors and committee members) to attend the Municipal Council through a representative assembly. The term of the aforementioned representatives (directors and committee members) shall be one year, and they may be re-elected. However, at each representative assembly, a vote shall first be taken among the incumbent directors and committee members to retain three-fifths of the directors and four-sevenths of the committee members, and the remaining number shall be elected according to these rules." Passed. (H) The French Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association requested this association to amend its name; should it be amended? Resolved: The name shall be amended to the Shanghai Public Concession Chinese Ratepayers Association. (I) A temporary proposal by Wang Xiaolai urged the Chinese directors and committee members to diligently fulfill their duties. Resolved: Each director should attend all meetings of the Municipal Council, and those who fail to attend for three consecutive times shall receive a written warning from the association. Those who fail to attend after four times shall be subject to sanctions by the Executive Committee. After the discussion, the meeting adjourned with refreshments at 5:15 PM.

Letter to the Bureau for Review: The association sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday notifying them of the list of elected directors and committee members for this term. The original letter stated: "Dear Sirs, We hereby inform you that Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu, Jiang Yiping, Xi Yushu, and Guo Shun have been elected by the ratepayers' representative assembly as directors to attend your bureau for the 25th and 26th years of the Republic. Lin Kanghou, Zhu Wenqi, Xu Xiaochu, Yu Hualong, Chen Jicheng, and Zhou Yueran have been elected as committee members to attend your bureau for the aforementioned years. We enclose the contact information of the directors and committee members for your bureau's review and action." Letter to Directors and Committee Members Notifying of Election: "Dear Sirs, At the representative assembly of this term, Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu, Jiang Yiping, Xi Yushu, and Guo Shun were elected as directors of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council for the 25th and 26th years of the Republic. Lin Kanghou, Zhu Wenqi, Xu Xiaochu, Yu Hualong, Chen Jicheng, and Zhou Yueran were elected as committee members. Please be informed that we have notified the Municipal Council and submitted a report accordingly for your review and action."

Telegram to the Ministry for Record: The association sent a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the National Government in Nanjing yesterday requesting recordation, which read: "To Minister Zhang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing, At the ratepayers' representative assembly of this term, Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu, Jiang Yiping, Xi Yushu, and Guo Shun were elected as directors of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council for this year. Bank of Communications: Yesterday Held General Meeting of Shareholders; Net Profit of Over 1.29 Million Yuan for the 24th Year

The 25th General Meeting of Shareholders of the Bank of Communications was held at 3 PM yesterday in the conference room on the fifth floor of the Hong Kong Road Bankers' Association. Attendees included government shareholders' representatives Tang Shoumin, Song Ziliang, Xi Demao, Chen Hang, Zhang Shoumin, and commercial shareholders Hu Bijang, Qian Xinzhi, Hu Mengjia, Xu Xinliu, Shen Shuyu, Li Fuxun, Qin Runqing, Zhou Zuomin, Ye Fuxiao, Yang Desen, Wang Zhixin, and over a hundred others, chaired by Hu Bijang, Chairman of the Board.

Meeting Proceedings: After the bell rang to commence the meeting, Chairman Hu Bijang first reported that the shares represented at today's General Meeting of Shareholders amounted to 14,509,100 yuan, which met the legal quorum for the meeting to proceed. After leading the attendees in a formal greeting, he reported on the business situation for the 24th year. Next, Director Zhuang Shuhou of the Auditing Department reported on the business accounts, and Supervisor Xu Xiudao reported that there were no discrepancies in the audit of the accounts. Afterwards, bank staff reported on the proposal to increase the savings fund and allocate another credit fund. The report also covered the amendment to the bank's articles of association, which was passed by the previous general meeting of shareholders and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for instructions. Proposals were then put forward regarding: The profit distribution plan for the 25th year. The proposal to deposit savings reserve funds. Both were passed as proposed.

Business Report: The bank's business situation for the 24th year was as follows: The total outstanding balance of deposits was over 33,147,400 yuan, an increase of over 89,427,000 yuan compared to the previous year. The outstanding balance of fixed deposits was over 7,620,000 yuan, the outstanding balance of current deposits was over 14,403,000 yuan, and the outstanding balance of cashier's checks and miscellaneous deposits was over 11,244,000 yuan. The total amount of outward remittances was over 45,704,900 yuan, an increase of over 16,600,700 yuan compared to the previous year. The total amount of purchased drafts was over 29,331,800 yuan, an increase of over 11,164,100 yuan compared to the previous year. This was a significant improvement, as the bank has always focused on facilitating remittances to support the flow of industrial finance. During the year, branches and offices continued to be established, the distribution of remittance locations was further expanded, and efforts were made to simplify procedures and improve convenience for customers. Since the currency system was changed, remittances throughout the country have been free of any water adjustment, making turnover more flexible and achieving some success. The total outstanding balance of loans and investments was over 25,467,800 yuan, an increase of over 39,786,000 yuan compared to the previous year. The outstanding balance of fixed loans was over 6,369,500 yuan, remaining at about the same level as the previous two years. The outstanding balance of current loans was over 15,028,800 yuan, an increase of over 19,329,000 yuan compared to the previous year. The outstanding balance of discounted loans was over 5,942,000 yuan, similar to the previous year. The outstanding balance of marketable securities was over 34,751,000 yuan, an increase of over 11,380,000 yuan compared to the previous year. Excluding marketable securities, the total outstanding balance of fixed loans, current loans, and discounted loans was over 21,992,500 yuan, an increase of over 28,405,000 yuan compared to the previous year. The increase was mainly due to loans secured by goods and factory sites, followed by loans secured by securities, and then loans to institutions and organizations. The bank's lending practices have always emphasized credit based on collateral. In addition to adding warehouses to directly undertake cargo pledges this year, it also focused on industrial and agricultural loans. Therefore, the increase in cargo pledges alone was significant, and factory site pledges also saw some success. The net profit was over 1,290,900 yuan, an increase of over 383,000 yuan compared to the previous year. The interest and handling fees accounted for the majority of the income, totaling over 6,331,000 yuan. As for expenses, various expenses increased slightly with the development of business, totaling over 3,619,000 yuan. In addition, depreciation of real estate and property was allocated separately according to past practice, totaling over 963,000 yuan. Bad debts totaled over 137,000 yuan, and issuance tax totaled over 310,900 yuan. The total expenses were over 5,040,900 yuan. After offsetting the income and expenses, the net profit was over 1,290,900 yuan. The total amount of banknotes in circulation, excluding banknotes from Liaoning and Harbin and other old banknotes that were only received but not issued, was 18,082,560 yuan, an increase of 7,759,800 yuan compared to the previous year. The cash reserve was 11,762,183 yuan, accounting for over 65% of the circulating amount. The guarantee reserve was 6,320,03817 yuan, accounting for just under 35% of the circulating amount. In terms of the annual issuance situation, although there was a decline in the slow months of February, April, and May, as in previous years, it gradually increased after June. By the end of October, it was comparable to the highest amount at the end of the previous year. Since the implementation of the new currency system in November, the bank's banknotes have been designated as legal tender, and the amount in circulation has been strengthened.

Administrative Report: Regarding administrative reforms and various tasks, the important ones are as follows: In March of this year, the bank was ordered by the government to amend the Bank of Communications regulations, changing the total amount of the bank's capital to 20 million yuan in national currency and expanding government shares by 12 million yuan, which has been fully allocated. All dividend ratios and the number of supervisors have been revised. The government has also granted special permission for the bank to be a bank that develops national industry. The types of business have not changed significantly and are still entrusted by the government to handle various matters and may be entrusted by the Central Bank. The bank's responsibilities have become even more important, and its capital strength has doubled. As for the bank's amended articles of association, the previous general meeting of shareholders has already discussed and passed them. Subsequently, the Ministry of Finance ordered the revision and approval for record. In recent years, the promotion of business has been based on the principle of assisting industry and balancing finance between urban and inland areas. The expansion of the business network is mainly in the coastal and railway lines. The business institutions in the Shaanxi, Shanxi, Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong areas have been continuously developed or appropriately adjusted. The branch offices in the Northeast have been reorganized or directly abolished in accordance with the times. Over thirty new banks, credit departments, and sub-departments were opened this year. Warehouses have also continued to increase this year. The newly opened warehouses include those in Hanyang, Changsha, Ningbo, Wuxi, Huangqiao, Qingjiangpu, Bengbu, and Suiyuan. The remaining construction projects are underway. In addition to the former construction of the Harbin, Hailar, Dalian, and Yantai branches, the Changshu branch and the Shanghai warehouse have also been completed one after another. The bank buildings under construction this year include those in Xuzhou and Gulangyu. There are also warehouses in Bengbu, Ningbo, Xi'an, and Weinan. More than half of the construction projects have been completed, and the purchase of land and the design and construction are underway in more than one or two locations. This year, from spring to autumn, domestic industry was stimulated by international financial policies, and there was panic due to rural disasters. The currency was tight, and business declined. In early November, stimulated by currency reform, the dynamics of the industrial sector gradually became active, but the purchasing power of the people did not increase. Industry and commerce still need to be strengthened. The bank's mission is to develop industry, and it should provide appropriate assistance in this environment. Over the past year, the bank has worked with the government on projects such as the silk industry improvement plan, the preparation and control of the fishing industry, and the regional management of agricultural credit cooperatives. It has also paid particular attention to expanding export businesses. In terms of industry and commerce, it has provided loans to textile factories, flour mills, and chemical factories to help them expand their operations if they are expected to make progress but lack working capital. For larger projects that require comprehensive planning, it has assisted in designing reasonable plans or issuing corporate bonds for the bank to underwrite, so as to promote their self-reliance and complete the bank's mission of assisting and regulating the economy. In recent years, the government has been boldly advancing construction projects. All aspects of road repair and water conservancy projects have been planned with foresight and actively implemented. The bank has a long-standing and historical relationship with these projects. Over the past year, the bank has spared no effort to support the connection of the Jiangnan Railway and the Jingwu Line, the extension of the Longhai Railway's Xibao section, the construction of the Xiangqian Highway, the Zhunhe project, and the dredging of the Yellow River's water conservancy, all of which improve people's livelihoods and promote production. As for projects that have not yet been completed, such as the construction of the Qiantang River Bridge, the diversion of the Wei River, and the development of the Huainan Railway Coal Mine, the bank will continue to provide assistance according to the original plans. This year, after the start of the Lunar New Year, the bank recognized that Shanghai's finance is the lifeblood of the country and cannot be ignored. It cooperated with the Central Bank and the Bank of China to provide interbank lending to various banks to facilitate turnover. It also purchased silver from Hong Kong and London to provide assistance. The panic in the market was initially relieved. When the market became tight again during the Spring Festival, the government took emergency measures to provide relief, and the bank joined with other banks to form a syndicate to provide lending. It also worked with the Bank of China to serve as a clearinghouse for concentrated exchange of bills, adjusting the holdings of various banks and financiers. It was able to barely survive the crisis. From August onwards, the bank cooperated with other banks to provide industrial and commercial credit, which was used as a more general form of adjustment. The bank's banknotes were designated as legal tender, and society's expectations of the bank became even stronger. The bank also followed the government's policy, adjusting the situation in various local markets to promote the implementation of the currency system and establish a solid foundation. The trust business has already handled services such as the custody of securities, agency insurance, and the leasing of real estate. This year, as society's need for trust services has gradually increased, and the trust business is related to the bank's special mission of developing industry, the bank has specially formulated trust articles of association and submitted them to the Ministry for record. The trust fund is also planned to be allocated separately and managed independently, and it will be implemented gradually according to the needs of various branches. As for the future direction of efforts, there are about six points: Focus on mortgages to regulate the market's finance. Focus on corporate bonds to support productive enterprises. Support export businesses to adjust foreign trade. Expand inland business to support the rural economy. Increase the number of new warehouses to facilitate production and sales. Develop the trust business to complete the task of serving society. The first three items belong to the use of funds, and the last three items belong to the promotion of business, all based on the principle of circulating the finance of various industries and cultivating production and sales capabilities. In this time of economic decline, although we dare not predict the extent of the success, we must strive to achieve it with unity.

Yu Qiaqing Telegraphs Request to Exempt Whole Tax on Broken Rice

Yu Qiaqing of the Ningbo Association in Shanghai telegraphed Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance, stating: "To Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, The people of Ningbo are facing a food crisis. The association has previously dispatched representatives to meet with President Jiang to request a solution and to issue tax-exempt passports to facilitate relief. Subsequently, the Ningbo Food Management Committee ordered the rice industry to purchase sufficient quantities. As such, 5,500 tons of foreign broken rice was ordered to provide affordable rice for the poor. The rice industry has registered with the government. Recently, a ministry order has been issued stating that, starting from April 11th, imported foreign broken rice will be taxed at the same rate as whole rice, resulting in a doubled tax burden on the broken rice ordered by Ningbo. Therefore, we telegraph to request that the minister review and order the Zhejiang Customs to continue to tax the registered broken rice for Ningbo at the old rate and to reply via telegram. Yu Qiaqing et al. of the Ningbo Association respectfully bow."

Lin Yi'shun's Coffin Transported to Beijing Yesterday Morning

The coffin of Lin Yi'shun, a revolutionary pioneer and overseas Chinese from Nanyang, was moved from the Universal Funeral Home on Jiaozhou Road to the North Station at 6:30 AM yesterday. No ceremonial guards were used along the way. At 7:55 AM, a special carriage was added to the fourth Shanghai-Beijing express train for transport to Beijing. A white cloth banner reading "The Coffin of Mr. Lin Yi'shun, a Pioneer of the Party and Nation, Being Transported to Beijing for Public Burial" was hung on the carriage. The Shanghai Public Security Bureau band also arrived to play music in tribute. Those accompanying the coffin to Beijing, in addition to Lin Yi'shun's son, Lin Minchang, included Feng Ziyou, Zhang Yongfu, Shao Fei, Zhang Huadan, Shao Jun, and over twenty others. Mayor Wu specially dispatched Li Dachao to the station to see off the coffin and take care of everything. The carriage is expected to arrive in Beijing at 1:50 PM and will be temporarily stored at the Renxiao Funeral Home on Moshou Road. His son will return to Shanghai from Singapore in a week and will come north again with his family when the date of the public burial is set.

Zhejiang Provincial Government Replies to the All-Zhejiang Public Association Regarding the Issuance of New Public Bonds

The All-Zhejiang Public Association received a reply telegram from the Zhejiang Provincial Government, which read: "To the All-Zhejiang Public Association in Shanghai, We have received and read your esteemed telegram of the day. The Zhejiang Provincial Finance is facing a severe deficit and is on the verge of collapse. The debt service expenses for the 25th year of the Republic have increased to over 11 million yuan, exceeding one-half of the annual revenue. The debt service cannot be reduced according to the agreements, and the various administrative expenses are difficult to cut. Furthermore, in this time of rural bankruptcy and social economic decline, there is no way to open up new sources of tax revenue. The disparity between income and expenditure is so great that a budget cannot be prepared. Moreover, the provincial treasury's existing financial resources are definitely unable to bear this huge debt. To alleviate the current difficulties and stabilize future credit, there is no other way but to reorganize all debts. Although the silver and money industries in this province may have slightly different views on the extension of bond deadlines and interest rate reductions, they have now understood after clear explanations. We deeply appreciate your concern for your hometown and your enthusiastic support. Your suggestion to use the original bond funds of this province as collateral to consult with the Ministry of Finance and order the Central Bank to lend legal tender at low interest rates to fully recover the originally issued bonds is a very good solution. The Ministry of Finance has also considered this plan, but the Central Bank of China and the Bank of Communications still need to provide cash reserves in accordance with the regulations for issuing legal tender, making it difficult to negotiate a resolution. Finance Director Cheng has gone to Beijing to consult with the Ministry of Finance and implement the plan accordingly. We know of your concern and are providing this update. We hope you understand. Governor Huang Shaoji of the Zhejiang Provincial Government."

The Shanghai International Settlement Inspects the Shanghai Volunteer Corps Yesterday; Troops from Various Nationalities Participate, Totaling Over 1,500; An Annual Banquet Held at the Shanghai Volunteer Corps Club That Evening

The Shanghai International Settlement's Shanghai Volunteer Corps held its annual grand inspection at 3:30 PM yesterday at the Shanghai Race Club (formerly known as "Club Concordia", now demolished) in front of the Shanghai Race Club on Nanjing West Road (formerly Bubbling Well Road). All infantry, cavalry, artillery, engineering, and transport units of various nationalities participated. Officials and individuals from various countries, exceeding ten thousand, attended as spectators. The details are as follows:

Inspection Details: A large viewing stand was specially erected in front of the Shanghai Race Club beforehand. The central section was reserved for the Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) directors, with the commander's platform directly facing the road in front. Seating to the left was designated for officials from various countries, while the sidewalks on both sides and opposite were for general guests. Officers specially dispatched by the Shanghai Municipal Police, along with the Shanghai Volunteer Corps' special forces, maintained order at the scene. As each unit passed the commander's platform, they all turned left, goose-stepping, and saluted the SMC Chairman, Arnold, the British military commander, Sackville, and the Shanghai Volunteer Corps Commander, Greighan, on the commander's platform. The infantry commands of various national units were all modeled after their home country's style, using their native language, in a variety of forms, creating a spectacular scene. Pedestrians stopped to watch.

Attendees: Those present at the time included SMC Chairman Arnold, Vice-Chairman Fenckling, Directors Yu Qiaqing, Xi Yushu, Bode, MacKnoden, as well as Director-General Fessenden and Director-General Chung En, in addition to Songhu Garrison Commander Yang Hu, Chief of Staff Xu Jinyuan, Aide-de-Camp Mi Xi, Shanghai Security Corps Commander Ji Zhangjian, Sir Frederick Leith-Ross, the British Economic Advisor specially dispatched to China, Inspector General of Customs Frederick Maze, British Consul-General Brenan, American Consul-General Gauss, French Consul-General Badas, Italian Consul-General Nielon, Russian Consul-General Spivana, German Consul-General Kliefeker, Norwegian Consul-General Or, Swedish Consul-General Beche Ferry, Danish Consul-General Heer, Swiss Consul-General Liechten, Brazilian Consul-General Branca, U.S. Marine Corps Commander Beaumont, French Army Commander Bertier, Japanese Marine Corps Commander Kondo, consuls-general and military attachés from various countries, as well as people from all sectors of society, both Chinese and foreign, and spectators along the way, totaling no less than ten thousand people.

Order of March: During the inspection, various units advanced in order, led by the military band of the British Army's Lancashire Regiment. The order was as follows: Headquarters, Cavalry, Headquarters, Light Horse, U.S. Company Signal Corps, Infantry A Battalion, Battalion Headquarters, A Company, B Company, Scottish Company, Jewish Company, Anti-Aircraft Company, Infantry B Battalion, Battalion Headquarters, U.S. Company, Portuguese Company, Filipino Company, U.S. Machine Gun Company, Infantry C Battalion, Battalion Headquarters, First Company, Second Company, Third Company, Fourth Company, Corps Lumberyard Cover Team, Japanese Company, Chinese Company, Interpreter Team, Transport Team, White Russian Company, Mechanized Unit, Armored Car Company, Artillery Company, Company Headquarters, Light Artillery Company, Heavy Artillery Company, Engineering Company, Field Team, Service Company, Transportation Company, Cook Squad, totaling over one thousand five hundred people.

Route: The mechanized unit first assembled and departed from the Shanghai Municipal Council Shanghai Volunteer Corps Training Room at 2:30 PM, gathering at Ma Huo Road. Other units assembled and departed from the racecourse at 3:20 PM. The inspection time was 3:30 PM. Traffic on Nanjing West Road (formerly Bubbling Well Road) between Ma Huo Road and Carter Road was temporarily cut off. After passing through the inspection grounds, the mechanized unit turned onto Nanjing West Road, then onto Haig Road, then past Avenue Foch, Avenue Edward VII, Xizang Road, turning into Hankou Road, and returning to the Shanghai Volunteer Corps Training Room. The remaining units returned to the racecourse via Weihaiwei Road, lasting over an hour.

Evening Banquet: After the inspection, a grand annual banquet was held at the Shanghai Volunteer Corps Club on Fuzhou Road at 7:00 PM that evening. All officers and soldiers attended to celebrate together. SMC Chairman Arnold, Inspection Officer British Army Commander Sackville, and Superintendent of the Shanghai Municipal Police were also invited.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Requests Jiangsu Construction Bureau to Reimburse Funds Advanced for Dredging the Wusong River

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, formerly the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, borrowed funds from the Nantao Branch of the China United Trading Corporation on behalf of the Wusong River Conservancy Association to dredge the Wusong River. Having not yet been reimbursed, yesterday, it sent a letter to the Jiangsu Construction Bureau requesting that it arrange for reimbursement and that it inform the China United Trading Corporation of the progress. The original letter stated:

Letter to the Jiangsu Construction Bureau: In regards to the former Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, in January of the 13th year of the Republic (1924), to refuse the Dredging Bureau being led by foreign consultants, joined the Shanghai, Baoshan, Jiading, Qingpu, Taicang, Kunshan, Wuxian, and Wujiang eight-county legal entities to organize the Wusong River Conservancy Association, submitted a report to the former Jiangsu Provincial Governor's Office, approved for filing, raised funds for independent dredging. In August of the 13th year, construction began on the section east of New Gate Bridge to the mouth of the river, completed in May of the 15th year. At that time, donations from the eight counties were either overturned mid-negotiation, diverted for other uses due to cases, or delayed due to hesitation. At that time, Fang Jifan, the vice president of the Wusong River Conservancy Association, was also the vice president of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce. Therefore, the deficit in the funds for that section of the project was borrowed from banks in the city by the vice president to meet the construction needs. The banks, considering that the Wusong River Conservancy Association was newly formed, while the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce had a long history, made the loans with the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce as the counterparty. Therefore, the main body of this loan for dredging the Wusong River seems to belong to the association, but in reality, it is directly the responsibility of the former General Chamber of Commerce. In January of the 17th year of the Republic (1928), the Wusong River Conservancy Association, considering that the eastern section was completed, and the eight-county legal entities, such as county councils, could no longer exist according to the law, lacking anyone responsible, and having no hope for continued work, immediately submitted a report to your bureau requesting a declaration of dissolution and a request to return the advanced funds. On January 31st of that year, Instruction No. 298 from your bureau stated that the funds advanced by the association should be comprehensively planned again and other methods discussed. Subsequently, on February 17th, March 27th, February of the 18th year, May 15th, December 18th of the 18th year, January 9th, January 29th, May 19th of the 19th year, May 25th of the 20th year, December 27th of the 22nd year, the association submitted reports to your bureau urging immediate reimbursement. In the association's reports, the most crucial phrases include, "Those who embezzled public funds are able to hide and protect themselves, while those who suffered losses for public affairs have no way to seek redress, inevitably causing those who take on responsibilities to lose heart and despair, and the difficult situation is recounted with tears." Also, Instruction No. 2994 from your bureau in June of the 19th year to the association stated that for this fund, only Wuxian County had remitted 12,000 yuan in total, while the other counties were either delaying remittance or had not determined a method, and that disbursement should wait until a large amount of funds had been remitted and the methods of the other counties had been determined. Subsequently, on March 30th of the 23rd year, your bureau instructed the association, stating that although the Wusong River dredging funds of the various counties had been cleared in the past, they still had not been remitted, and according to the previous report, the Finance Department had been consulted to send personnel to re-clear and urge remittance, and that disbursement would be made after a certain amount had been remitted. Since then, the association has not received any further instructions from your bureau, but the bank has been urging payment for a long time, and its tone has gradually become stricter. Furthermore, the debt has been accumulating over time, with interest compounding, becoming increasingly large. In June of the 16th year of the Republic (1927), the outstanding principal and interest owed to the bank amounted to 87,754 yuan and 19 fen. By the end of December of the 24th year, it had reached 220,027 yuan. Such a heavy debt is certainly not in the interest of the public. Our association is suffering for others' mistakes and has no way to resolve it. We hereby request that your bureau, in accordance with the association's reports, earnestly take responsibility for arranging reimbursement, in the spirit of public cooperation.

Reply to China United Trading Corporation Nantao Branch: On the 11th of this month, we received your letter stating that the funds borrowed by the former General Chamber of Commerce from your bank for dredging the Wusong River have been outstanding for a long time and requesting that we find a way to resolve the matter. In this matter, your branch's letter to our association on November 6th of the 23rd year was most earnest, stating that "the reason our bank made this loan is a small matter for water conservancy and a large matter for sovereignty. Because our bank made the loan, Chinese rights were protected, and the government should reward us." Therefore, the former General Chamber of Commerce's protection of the country and sovereignty was the same standpoint as your branch, and it has been understood. Therefore, our association replied on November 15th of that year, stating that "In general, the former General Chamber of Commerce handled this matter, as your letter said, for the sake of preserving sovereignty, and it is in the same situation as your bank, suffering for public affairs. Our association, inheriting the duties of the former four merchant groups, has also been urging the government to pay this advanced fund. I hope you will understand." Now that we have received your instructions, our association feels the same anxiety as your branch after many years, and what we can tell your branch is that we are still continuing to urge payment and dare not neglect it.

Three Instances of Extortion by Bandits at the Xingshan Nunnery in Zhabei

Buddhist nun Zhizhen, age 50, of Anhui province, is the abbess of the Xingshan Nunnery on Zhongxing Road, Song Park Road, Zhabei. The nunnery is usually quite prosperous, attracting the covetous attention of bandits. On the afternoons of the 15th, 16th, and 17th of this month, at 3:00 PM, 3:00 PM, and 3:30 PM respectively, a group of six or seven individuals went to the nunnery, pried open the gate with iron tools, rushed in, and threatened the young nuns to extort money. Fortunately, Abbess Zhizhen was out and had not returned. The group failed in their plot and left disgruntled. Afterwards, Nun Zhizhen reported the incident to the North Station Sub-Bureau. Yesterday afternoon at around 3:00 PM, Detective Squad Leader Gu Shucheng, Guo Mengqu, along with detectives Shen Jinchu, Zhou Jitang, Huai Xinmao, and others, together with officers dispatched by the New Gate Sub-Bureau, rushed to No. 5, Wufuli, Meiyuan Road, and arrested extortionist bandits Yin Huaiyu (age 25, from Funing) and Sun Wencai (age 38, from Yangzhou). After interrogation, the sub-bureau prepared a document to submit to the general bureau for investigation and prosecution, as the case concerned extortion and fraud.

Inside the Gu Zhuxuan Case: Conniving in the Case of Opium Addicts Jia and Wu Concluded; Prosecutor Argues for Permitting Opium Use; Debate Concluded; Judgment to be Announced on the 25th

After Gu Zhuxuan was detained by the Special Second Court for instigating an assassination and sentenced to fifteen years, during the appeal period, Gu bribed the guards outside the prison ward where he was being held and incited perjury. At the same time, prison guard supervisor Jia Furong and guard station supervisor Wu Lu connived with Gu to allow him to smoke opium in prison. The Second Section Chief of the Prison, Ouyang Sen, went to search and found opium residue, opium pipe stems, white powder, and cigarettes, among other evidence. After the prosecutor filed a public prosecution against them with the criminal court of the same court, various investigations were conducted, as reported in the previous issue. Yesterday afternoon, the malfeasance case against Jia Furong and Wu Lu was further investigated. Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu, along with Prosecutor Wang, came to the Second Criminal Court. First, the ages and origins of the two defendants, Jia and Wu, were asked, and then they were questioned separately. The prosecutor said to Jia Furong, "The High Third Court and the prison both have orders and announcements stating that they must assist in guarding prisoners in the external prison ward. Now, you are responsible for the prisoners. "Jia replied that as long as the prisoners do not escape, he is responsible. "How many people smoke opium in the external prison ward?" "I don't know if anyone smokes." "Then how did you find opium residue in Gu's room? How did it get in?" "I don't know the truth, and I didn't see it. If I had seen it, I wouldn't have been so careless." "How much money did you get?" "I have always been law-abiding and have never dared to be greedy." Wu Lu was then brought in. According to Wu's confession, he was assigned to the external prison ward on October 11th of last year to assist the prison guard. "Do you go into the prison cells?" "No, but the inspection is very strict. Every time I get off work, Jia Furong checks for me." "Did you see any opium during the inspection?" "I have never seen it." "Then why did prisoner Wang A'er say that you bought opium for Gu?" "In fact, Wang A'er and I have a grudge." Informants Li Heshang, Guo Shanyu, and Wang A'er were brought in and uniformly stated that Jia and Wu had connived with Gu Zhuxuan to allow him to smoke opium, but the civilians had no animosity against Jia and Wu. The rest of the testimony was the same as the previous hearing. The prosecutor ordered the debate to begin. First, Prosecutor Wang Ren stepped forward to argue, stating that the various accusers in this case unanimously identified the two defendants as conniving in permitting opium use, and that last year, Chief Ouyang, based on Wang A'er's report, went to search and found opium residue and opium pipes, which were sent to the Forensic Research Institute for examination. The results confirmed that there was opium use. Although it cannot be proven that the two defendants took bribes and bought opium, the fact that they permitted the prisoner to smoke opium is clear. He requested that they be investigated and prosecuted according to law. The lawyers for the two defendants then argued for a long time. Presiding Judge Wang then announced the conclusion of the debate and set the judgment for the afternoon of the 25th. Jia Furong was still entrusted to the warden for custody, and Wu Lu and the accusers were returned to prison.

Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association: The Opening Ceremony of the Third Fundraiser Convened Yesterday; Mayor Wu, Jordan, and 50 Others Attended; 100,000 Yuan Raised to Build the Qiaqing Anti-Tuberculosis Hospital

The Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association held the opening ceremony of its third fundraiser at the Eight Immortals Bridge YMCA at 4:00 PM yesterday. Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Jordan, the Chief Health Officer of the Shanghai Municipal Council, Lu Bohong, the Director of the Association, Li Tingan, the Director of the Health Bureau, and fundraising team leaders Yan Fuqing, Niu Huisheng, Jae Bochi, Ding Huikang, Xi Guansheng, Zhou Bangjun, Wu Yunxu, Liu Yide, Li Dachao, and about 50 others attended. They were divided into 55 teams for fundraising. In addition, in honor of the 70th birthday of Shanghai leader Yu Qiaqing on July 3rd of this year, the association plans to raise 100,000 yuan to build the Qiaqing Anti-Tuberculosis Hospital, which was also approved at yesterday's meeting. Various groups and individuals initiated the effort, and a committee for administrative design was elected to actively promote it. Lu Bohong had already purchased more than 60 mu of land near the North Bridge in Shanghai County for the foundation, and the groundbreaking ceremony is scheduled for July 3rd.

President's Speech: After the ceremony, President Lu Bohong delivered a speech, saying, "Ladies and gentlemen, today is the day to solicit members and raise funds. I have good news to tell you. I have been serving society for nearly thirty years, but I have never been able to complete an anti-tuberculosis hospital. This year, July 3rd, is the birthday of Shanghai leader Mr. Yu Qiaqing. Our association plans to take this opportunity to raise 100,000 to 200,000 yuan to build an anti-tuberculosis hospital, named 'Qiaqing Anti-Tuberculosis Hospital.' I have already purchased more than 60 mu of land near the North Bridge in Shanghai County, with a width of 850 feet and a depth of 450 feet. We plan to build it in nine sections, first building five sections, four sections for patients, and one section for doctors and offices. When all nine sections are completed, it can accommodate 1,000 patients. Currently, we have the land, but we lack the construction funds. Therefore, we plan to raise funds. We hope you will support us. As for the doctors, famous hospitals abroad have volunteered to assign them. Also, this year's membership drive aims to raise 15,000 yuan. We have hired 55 fundraising teams, each led by one person, and they have all agreed. This year, we plan to add tuberculosis clinics in various areas of the concessions."

Mayor Wu's Speech: "Ladies and gentlemen, I am sorry for arriving late due to an event today. This year, I was elected as the overall team leader of the fundraising event. Although I may not be able to spare much time to serve, this matter is important, so I dare not decline. Preventing tuberculosis in China is the most urgent matter. In the past, there was not only a lack of action but also a lack of understanding. We need to attach importance to this disease. New medicine has been in China for a long time, but generally, people only pay attention to tuberculosis when they cough up blood. With toothaches, people only think they're sick when they are in pain, and they don't think of it as a disease otherwise. In fact, toothaches without pain are more serious than those with pain. I didn't have this feeling before, but after I contracted it myself, I realized its importance. In this city, when we examine students' health, 80 out of 100 have a positive reaction to pulmonary tuberculosis, which makes them very likely to develop lung tuberculosis in the future. This is what the ordinary society does not pay attention to, and the government does not have the extra power to do. Three years ago, Mr. Niu Huisheng and others, aware of this, initiated this association. In the past three years, its work has been focused on propaganda and prevention. Recently, fundraising activities have gradually shown results. This time, we plan to build a defense hospital in honor of Mr. Yu Qiaqing's 70th birthday. Mr. Yu has served in Shanghai for 55 years, encouraging local business and sparing no effort. Therefore, we plan to commemorate him with this plan and benefit the local area. This is a win-win situation. This association is preparing to raise funds, and we ask for your assistance."

Speeches by Jordan and Yan: Chief Health Officer Jordan of the Shanghai Municipal Council then spoke, saying, "Shanghai's health implementation work, such as treatment and prevention, I am an official of the concessions, and I will do my best. Over the past few years, health implementation has made progress. I represent the Shanghai Municipal Council in thanking the social leaders for their help. Today, I heard that an anti-tuberculosis hospital will be built, and I hope it can be completed soon." Yan Fuqing then spoke, saying, "In the past two or three years, after difficult work where spending money didn't seem effective, this association has gradually made progress. This association is an organization jointly initiated by the government and society. The government promotes it, society works hard, and the results are effective. This association currently has three full-time staff members who handle daily affairs. We have also hired a full-time doctor to set up clinics and assist nurses. Tuberculosis prevention requires hospitals and doctors, which is very difficult. Patients need long-term treatment and attention to diet. Therefore, no one has ever done it. I have set up a lung disease sanatorium in Yeyuan, Jiangwan, with 150 beds. Those who are treated must stay for at least three months to half a year. There are more than 300 people who want to come in, but there is no way to accommodate them, so they are temporarily staying at the Zhabei Clinic. As soon as there is an opportunity, they rush to the hospital first, which shows the suffering of the patients. Now, there is a large-scale anti-tuberculosis hospital, and I hope to see it completed soon." Zhou Bangjun then spoke (omitted).

Hospital Plan: Mayor Wu then immediately led the planning and construction of the anti-tuberculosis hospital and assigned the work methods, which were determined in public: Name: Yu Qiaqing 70th Birthday Preparatory Committee (established for fundraising for the Qiaqing Anti-Tuberculosis Hospital); Initiation: Initiated by various groups and individuals; Grouping: A, Anti-Tuberculosis Hospital Administrative Committee; B, Anti-Tuberculosis Hospital Design Committee; Committee Members: Administrative Committee: Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Qian Xinzhi, Lin Kanghou, Liu Hongsheng, Yu Zuoting, Lu Bohong, Li Dachao; Design Committee: Yan Fuqing, Li Tingan, Ding Huikang, Lu Bohong, Shen Yi, Dong Dayou, Jordan, Dr.J.H.Jordan; Purpose: To raise 100,000 yuan.

Each team will have one team leader, a deputy team leader, and several team members; Rewards: 1.
