Confessions of a Working Woman

Female Nurse

— Interview with Ms. He Jiren

To be honest, my purpose in studying nursing was not initially because the profession had a charitable nature, but because it was a relatively easy way to find a job, so I spent three years and earned the title of nurse.

In the summer of the year of the Republic, I took a diploma from a certain girls' middle school, and with this qualification, I managed to pass the examination and enter a hospital sponsored by a church in the South City to study nursing. I studied there for half a year and paid 50 yuan in tuition fees. Because I was not interested in religion, I dropped out halfway. Fortunately, a relative who had just returned from studying in the United States introduced me to a charity hospital in Shanghai to continue my studies. The rules and organization there were better than those of the church hospital. There was also a school, with teachers for each department. After I went there, I could go out for one Sunday a week. As for class time, it was from 8:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m. every day, which was the same as ordinary schools.

Time passed like flowing water, and the six months of studying passed unconsciously. From then on, I began my internship. The first time I was assigned to work in the women's ward No. 3. There were seven or eight patients there, each suffering from different ailments, and each with a different temperament.

"Miss X, are you on duty? That's great! Let me tell you, there aren't many things to do here. If you don't have time, you can ask for help. However," she took a step closer and whispered in my ear, "Don't show that you're new in front of the patients, otherwise the patients will 'bully the newcomer'!"

She walked away with a smile. Many patients looked at me. Although I felt a little uneasy in my heart at this time, I couldn't show it on my face. After a while, a patient shouted, "Nurse, please cover me with this quilt."

I hurried over and helped her cover the quilt.

"Nurse, I want to get up. Please help me." Another patient's voice.

I knew she wanted to get up to urinate, but I had never done this for anyone before, so I felt a little hesitant.

"Nurse, hurry up, I want to get up!"

The voice was louder than before. I knew that I had to go. Enduring a belly full of unwillingness, I uncovered the quilt for her: "Okay to get up?"

"No, I can't. My waist hurts so much. Please bring that thing."

I took a glass urinal and put it on her bed, and helped her up. I stared at her, but she kept sitting there like a wooden puppet for five or six minutes, as if she didn't notice that I was standing next to her.

"Are you done yet? My hand is sore and I can't hold it!" I complained a little.

"Oh! Why are you so impatient, nurse? It's not that easy to take care of patients!" She sounded like she had been hospitalized for a long time.

"Nurse, please give me some water to drink."

Just after serving one patient, I hurried to the other side. Like a tea servant, I couldn't always be there, but when I heard a patient calling, I had to answer.

"It's too cold, this water. Nurse, you try it too. Can patients drink such cold water?" She put the bowl on the chair hard.

Although there were only seven patients in the women's ward No. 3, it was more tiring than entertaining hundreds of guests at a school art show. This day, I worked from 11:00 a.m. to 6:00 p.m. The seven hours of work were not very long, but I was so tired after work that I even gave up dinner.

After I started my internship, I still had four hours of classes every day, so on the second morning of my internship in the ward, I still had to go to class.

"XX! Yesterday, the first time you went to intern, a patient complained that you didn't take good care of her. You're absolutely not allowed to do that again! Nurses should take care of patients as if they were taking care of their own family members, and serve them wholeheartedly. You have to be gentle and not afraid of being dirty. These conditions are indispensable for being a nurse, do you understand?" This was a head nurse, and she said a burst of words like popping beans after class, with a stern face.

After being scolded, I felt extremely wronged in my heart, but I didn't dare to argue. After the head nurse left, I told an old nurse about what happened yesterday, and she also taught me a lot of experience. She said: "A sick person is almost like a child. Sometimes they simply don't have any reason. When a nurse encounters this kind of person, they can only try to be patient. Whatever they want, as long as it doesn't violate the doctor's instructions, just give it to them. For example, yesterday a patient complained that the water was too cold. This can be said to be common, because there won't be that much hot water in the hospital. Even if there is hot water sometimes, those timid patients will still complain that it is too cold. So when you encounter this kind of patient, you can only 'endure' to subdue them. Like yesterday, a patient in ward No. 4 had a fever. He was given a lot of cold water to drink, but he still said that he was burning uncomfortably and asked for more cold water. Imagine, if these two patients lived in the same room, wouldn't that be troublesome to death?"

Being a nurse really requires "patience". If I didn't still have some "patience", I'm afraid I wouldn't have been able to continue working at that time. The reason is that I was assigned to work in the men's ward in front after working in the women's ward No. 3 for a short time. The number of people in that ward was the same as in the women's ward, but it was more difficult to take care of the male patients than the female patients.

According to hospital regulations, the patients' temperature must be measured with a thermometer several times a day. However, some patients show an attitude of annoyance when they see the nurse coming with the thermometer, and some even pretend to be asleep to ignore you. Some patients are already asleep, so you have to tiptoe and gently put the thermometer under their armpits like a thief. When I first came here to take care of patients, I thought there was no difference between taking care of female patients and taking care of male patients. How could I know that after only one week of work, I gained a lot of experience. Some patients deliberately thought of many things to ask me. Sometimes it seemed as if they had made an appointment in advance to joke with me. For example, the patients lying on beds No. 3 and No. 7 had very mild illnesses, but that day, when I came to take care of them for the first time, they pretended to be very serious, shouting for water and shouting for "urine". However, male patients' "urination and defecation" are usually taken care of by the tea servant, so I shouted for the tea servant and went to get water for another patient. However, the patient who wanted to "urinate" saw that I only shouted for the tea servant and did not go there himself. His illness seemed to have healed in that second. He sat up in one fell swoop. Later, the tea servant ran over, but his "urine" was gone. In my months of internship, I indeed "learned" a lot about patients like this. However, it cannot be said that there were no "well-behaved" patients, but these were mostly elderly people or people with lung diseases.

There is also a terrible thing that I have to mention here:

I remember that it was one winter night, around 11 o'clock. The patients in the room I was nursing were already asleep, and the air was as quiet as an ancient temple. I was just looking down at a medicine book when the glass door suddenly opened. I thought it was blown open by the wind. When I looked up, I was so scared that I couldn't speak for a long time. It turned out that the person pushing the door was a male patient, with several layers of gauze thickly wrapped around his head, even covering his eyes. He pushed the door open and was still groping into my ward. Although I was startled at the time, I didn't panic. I quickly flashed past him and ran outside to call several tea servants to carry the patient away like a chicken. However, I heard early the next morning that the man had already been placed in the "morgue". It turned out that his head had been injured by a car and he had ended his life less than ten hours after being taken to the hospital. Last night, because the nurse in that ward had just left for a while, he had secretly walked out.

After being a nurse for three years, my heart is as hard as iron. Many people always criticize nurses in this way. In fact, according to my personal experience, it is not the case. For example, in my six months of internship, it can be said that I simply did not eat a good meal or sleep soundly once. However, later, because of the endless pressure of life, you can't help but be a "tolerant person".

The duties of a nurse are so arduous, but the treatment received is inversely proportional to the duties. After being in the hospital for six months, I only received a subsidy of two yuan per month. By the third year, it was only increased by two yuan. After graduation, I had to volunteer for the hospital for three months. After the service period expired, if the hospital could continue to employ you, you could be considered a formal nurse, but the monthly salary was only twenty-four yuan.
